<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

	<section class="tab-pane pure-u-1-1 u-printing-display-inline-ie u-printing-display-inline-ff">
		<!-- ngIf: vm.loading -->
		<!-- ngIf: !vm.loading --><div ng-if="!vm.loading" class="ng-scope">
			<!-- uiView: --><div ui-view="" class="ng-scope"><section class="pure-u-1-1 document-abstract document-tab u-p-2 ng-isolate-scope" mathjax-bind="" id="6742640">

	<div class="pure-g">
		<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage --><div ng-if="::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage" ng-class="vm.details.graphicalAbstract ? 'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1' : 'pure-u-1-1'" class="ng-scope pure-u-1-1">
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement -->
		<!--/div-->
		<!--div ng-class="{'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1':  vm.details.graphicalAbstract, 'pure-u-1-1': ! vm.details.graphicalAbstract}"-->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This paper presents the development and demonstration of a high-efficiency rectifier for millimeter-wave-to-dc energy conversion. It is a critical circuit block that renders possible the use of a single CMOS chip die with no substrate and wiring, as the implementation of a batteryless, yet active tag for next-generation high data-rate millimeter-wave identification technologies. We also propose an architecture of a reader-tag system that addresses the underlying technical challenges. The rectifier is based on a differential drive cross-coupled topology that has been shown to work at UHF frequencies only so far. In this paper, we investigate significant challenges in implementing this topology at millimeter-wave frequencies with good power conversion efficiency (PCE). The analyses, design, and results presented in this work demonstrate the feasibility of achieving this by minimizing simultaneously the small on-resistance and the reverse leakage current in the MOS transistors, and by reducing losses and parasitic capacitances through proper transistor sizing and layout optimization. Using a standard 65-nm bulk CMOS process, a chip was designed, fabricated, and tested under different input and output loading conditions. The rectifier exhibits an overall PCE of 20% at 24 GHz, 18% at 35 GHz, and 11% at 60 GHz under RF available driving power of 6, 6, and 3 dBm, respectively, and output load resistance of 1, 1, and 2 kΩ, respectively. These PCE performances at millimeter-wave frequencies have never been reported in the literature.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->

<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>As AN emerging technology, RF identification (RFID) is being increasingly used in many areas of our everyday life, such as access control, security, and supply chain management. However, the restricted standard rules, tag size (mainly dominated by antenna), and limited data rate dictated by available bandwidths have impeded the evolution of the UHF RFID applications. Driven by ever-increasing needs, such as smaller size and higher data rates, RFID technology has entered into the millimeter-wave era to exploit the inherently smaller antenna size and larger available bandwidths <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. Batteryless millimeter-wave identification (MMID) becomes only possible if a tag can be powered wirelessly and it still benefits from these advantages at millimeter-wave frequencies. However, to the best of our knowledge, such MMID has not been reported yet. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, a standard UHF RFID chip is combined with external mixers to up-convert the transmit-UHF signal to 10 GHz and down-convert the received 10-GHz signal to the UHF, with a 40-kbit/s data rate. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, a 60-GHz RFID tag design is reported, but the low RF-to-dc power conversion efficiency (PCE) (1.2% at 2-dBm input power) translates into a bit-by-bit sequential communication, limiting the data rate to 5 kbit/s at a range of 1.3 cm.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6782344/6742640/6742640-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6782344/6742640/6742640-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig>Illustration of a reader-tag RFID system using backscattering.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6742640/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
A major challenge in developing a passive MMID is that the backscattering modulation technique generally used in passive UHF RFIDs performs poorly at millimeter-wave frequencies. As depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, in a backscattering passive RFID system, a reader continuously sends a high power signal to power up the tag, while listening to a very weak reflected signal, sent by the tag with a form of amplitude modulation as a result of the impedance switching of its own antenna. The signal received by the reader consists of two sidebands carrying the tag information, and a carrier tone level that is augmented by the reader's transmitter leakage signal and its associated sideband noise. This impacts negatively the reader sensitivity, but is acceptable in UHF RFIDs. However, the weaker backscattered signal at millimeter-wave frequencies (due to smaller tag-antenna aperture), as well as lower reader transmit–receive (TX–RX) isolation, higher phase noise in its millimeter-wave oscillator and low reader dynamic range <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a> compromise this modulation technique at millimeter-wave frequencies.<p></p><p>Therefore, batteryless “active” MMID technologies will benefit from a new reader-tag system that is free of backscattering.</p><p>In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>, a new MMID reader-tag system that is free of backscattering modulation is proposed at a conceptual level. The successful implementation of such a system, however, will require millimeter-wave-to-dc rectifiers with good PCE performances, e.g., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1000.66em 2.225em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/223C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 4px; vertical-align: 2px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: 0.07em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.403em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">\sim</script></tex-math></inline-formula>10% at 35 GHz under an RF input power of 6 dBm. To the best of our knowledge, a CMOS rectifier with such performances has never been reported in the literature. Note that published papers on millimeter-wave rectennas (e.g., <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>) make use of Schottky diodes and are intended for operation at significantly higher power levels than what is required in our applications.</p><p>In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>, we analyze and describe the design of a rectifier that was successfully tested using a commercial standard 65-nm CMOS process with measured PCE performances of 20%, 18%, and 11% at 24, 35, and 60 GHz, respectively. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a> presents and discusses the measurement results.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Proposed MMID System With Batteryless Tag</h2></div><p>The MMID reader-tag system proposed for batteryless “active” MMID tags, which does not require backscattering, is illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>. It uses two millimeter-wave frequencies, freq-1 for a continuous wave (CW) dedicated to energy source for the tag, and freq-2 for down and up-link communications only. Therefore, the reader interrogates and listens to the tag at anytime without interrupting the energy feed to the tag, hence without compromising the rectifier's PCE. Moreover, it eliminates the issue of charging and discharging synchronization stated in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_2">[3]</a>, as well as the issue of a reader sensitivity degradation associated with backscattering. This leads to a more relaxed coding and modulation methods, as well as higher data rates in both communication links.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6782344/6742640/6742640-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6782344/6742640/6742640-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig>Block diagram of the proposed MMID system with a batteryless active tag on single-chip.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6742640/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Previous works have reported millimeter-wave CMOS voltage-controlled oscillators (VCOs) with power consumption of few hundreds of microwatts despite a large tuning range <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2">[9]</a>, a dual-band on-chip antenna with 7.4- and 6.5-dBi gain at 35 and 94 GHz, respectively <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2">[10]</a>, and a clock generator consuming only 24 nW at 5.12 MHz <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2">[11]</a>. Besides, at UHF, the state-of-the art has shown fully integrated passive RFID transponders (including control logic and memory blocs) consuming less than 3-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-4" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.685em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.5em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-11" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0057.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 16px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\mu{\hbox{W}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dc power <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_2">[12]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]</a>. Assuming a 1-W effective isotropic radiation power (1-W EIRP) from a reader, a tag antenna gain of 6 dBi <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2">[10]</a>, and a conservatively high dc power of 500 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-12" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.685em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.5em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-18" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-19" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0057.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 16px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">\mu{\hbox{W}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dissipated by the MMID tag (excluding the rectifier), a power link budget analysis at 35 GHz using a Friis equation then shows that a 10% PCE is required for the rectifier to enable communication over 2 cm. With the design presented in this paper, we have measured a PCE of 18% at 35 GHz. This renders possible MMID systems as in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>, employing a batteryless “active” tag that is fully integrated on a single CMOS die, with no substrate, no die-attach, and no wiring.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Millimeter-Wave-To-DC Rectifier</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a> shows the rectifier schematic, based on a cross-coupled bridge topology that has been investigated at UHF only so far <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_3">[14]</a>. During the positive cycle of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-56" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.745em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.526em -999.997em); As long as an RF source is connected to the rectifier, transistors M1, M2, M3, and M4 will periodically charge <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-175" role="math" style="display: inline-block; (a) Differential-drive circuit schematic. (b) Equivalent capacitor model.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6742640/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The cross-coupled bridge topology allows a small on-resistance by biasing the nMOS (M2) in the saturation mode with a high gate voltage during the positive cycle of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-184" role="math" style="display: inline-block; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-185" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-186" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-188" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-189" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-190" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0052.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 8px; vertical-align: 0px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; It also allows reducing the unwanted source-to-drain reverse leakage current in M2 (due to the MOS symmetrical structure) during the negative cycle of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-192" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; At millimeter-wave frequencies, though, parasitic capacitances and series losses associated with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-208" role="math" style="display: inline-block; This will be analyzed in the following with the help of formulations from <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_3">[15]</a>.</p><p>As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a>, at millimeter-wave frequencies, the cross-coupled bridge topology implies a large parasitic capacitor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-225" role="math" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0068.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 6px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">V_{\rm th}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is beneficial to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1072" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.505em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1073" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1074" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1075" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0049.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1076" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1077" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1078" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0073.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1079" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 6px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1080" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0074.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">I_{\rm sat}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a>, but also implies a larger leakage current <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn6" href="#deqn6" class="fulltext-link">(6)</a>. Finally, a longer channel implies more parasitic capacitance <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn4" href="#deqn4" class="fulltext-link">(4)</a>, making the minimum usable <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1081" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.724em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1082" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1083" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/004C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">L</script></tex-math></inline-formula> the best design choice.</p><p>The above-described complex design tradeoffs show that a performant millimeter-wave rectifier design necessitates a thorough optimization. In this work, we aimed at optimizing the rectifier's PCE by simulation for best transistor and capacitor sizes as a function of the loading current. Note, however, that since a rectifier is a large-signal nonlinear circuit, a more robust optimization actually requires a much more complex procedure, such as what was proposed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3">[16]</a>, where source–pulling characterization is employed.</p><p>Our simulations showed that minimal transistor sizes yield an optimal design choice for our millimeter-wave rectifier. In addition, layout parasitic capacitances are critical for PCE. Hence, the distances between polysilicon gate, source, and drain contacts were optimized to reduce <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1084" role="math" style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">C_{\rm ds}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>In order to minimize capacitive coupling between metal traces, together with the associated losses, the transistors may be kept further apart to allow more distance between the metal traces. On the other hand, too long metal traces severely degrade the PCE because of excessive substrate losses. This aspect was taken into consideration during the layout design, through multiple iterations of post-layout simulation.</p><p>Series resistances Rs1 and Rs2 (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>) were added for test purposes in order to isolate the small <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1108" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 12px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1111" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1112" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1113" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">C{\rm load}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> capacitor from the bigger and lossy parasitic capacitors in the test pads.</p><p>Rs1 and Rs2 ensure that the RF signal flows through <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1117" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1134" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0064.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 6px; <div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Design and Measurement Results</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Chip Design and Measurement Setup</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> shows the die photograph of the fabricated test circuit with a chip area of 0.6 mm × 0.45 mm including RF pads, but with an active area of only <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1135" role="math" style="display: inline-block; The chip contains two rectifier design variants, one with narrower transistor and capacitor sizes [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(a)</a>] and the second with wider sizes [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(c)</a>], as well as a de-embedding bloc on the middle [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(b)</a>] for characterization and loss estimation for the input pads and transmission lines. The chip was fabricated using a standard 65-nm bulk CMOS technology, with regular-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1162" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1165" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1166" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1167" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0074.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1168" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0068.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6782344/6742640/6742640-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6782344/6742640/6742640-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig>Micrograph of the fabricated rectifier. <p></p><p>Transistor and capacitor sizes were optimized through simulation to obtain an approximated dc power of 500 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1169" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.685em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.5em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1170" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1171" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1172" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1173" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1174" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1175" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1176" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0057.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 16px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">\mu{\hbox{W}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as required for the active MMID tag. The narrower rectifier shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(a)</a> has W/L ratios of 1.2<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1177" role="math" style="display: inline-block; To minimize input losses, small and low-loss probing pads were used.</p><p>The rectifier was measured on-wafer with differential probes, and differentially driven using the true-mode stimulus application (TMSA) feature of Agilent N5247A PNA-X, to generate a true differential signal. A variable load resistor was connected to the output of the rectifier to emulate different dc power dissipated by an MMID tag. <p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Millimeter-Wave-to-DC Rectifier Performances</h3><p>Substrate losses measured after calibration show an insertion loss <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1343" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 4.928em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.447em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.39em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1344" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1345" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1346" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1347" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1348" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0032.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1349" style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.303em;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/003D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 4px; vertical-align: 2px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1350" style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1351" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1352" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1353" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0034.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0033.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">{S}12={S}43</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of 2.2 dB at 24 and 35 GHz, and 2.7 dB at 60 GHz. The results presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 5</a> – <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">7</a> were obtained with the design variant with wider transistors.</p><p>The measurements were carried out at three frequencies: 24, 35, and 60 GHz over a wide millimeter-wave band. The PCE dependence on the available input RF power (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1354" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.865em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.68em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1355" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1356" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1357" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1358" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0050.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.117em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1359" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1360" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1361" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1362" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0076.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6782344/6742640/6742640-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6782344/6742640/6742640-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig>Measured and simulated results at 35 GHz. <div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6782344/6742640/6742640-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6782344/6742640/6742640-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig>Measured and simulated results at 60 GHz. (a) PCE versus <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-99-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1456" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 2.384em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.855em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.26em 1001.86em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1457" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1458" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0050.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.129em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.136em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1459" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1460" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1461" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1462" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0076.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-99">P{\rm av}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (b) DC voltage versus <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-100-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1463" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 2.384em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.855em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.26em 1001.86em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1464" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1465" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0050.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.129em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.136em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1466" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1467" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1468" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1469" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0076.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-100">P{\rm av}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6742640/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 5(b)</a>, <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">6(b),</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">7(b)</a> show that at any frequency, the output dc voltage increases with the load resistance. This stems from the fact that a higher resistance draws less charge from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-101-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1470" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 2.646em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.345em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.35em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1471" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1472" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0043.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1473" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1474" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1475" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1476" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1477" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1478" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0064.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-101">C{\rm load}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which then maintains a higher voltage. This also explains why the PCE is lower with a larger load resistance, when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-102-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1479" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.865em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.68em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1480" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1481" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1482" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1483" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0050.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.117em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1484" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1485" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1486" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1487" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0076.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-102">{P{\rm av}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is in the upper range in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 5(a)</a>, <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">6(a)</a>, and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">7(a)</a>. The larger dc potential (with a larger resistance) at the drain terminal of M3, M4 [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a>] induces a higher reverse leakage current when either of these transistors is supposed to be off. This mechanism is less severe in the lower range of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-103-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1488" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.865em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.68em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1489" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1490" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1491" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1492" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0050.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.117em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1493" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1494" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1495" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1496" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0076.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-103">{P{\rm av}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where the losses due to currents into the transistors' channel resistances predominate. The lower load resistance then implies larger currents, translating into a lower efficiency in the lower range of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-104-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1497" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.865em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.68em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1498" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1499" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1500" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1501" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0050.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.117em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1502" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1503" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1504" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1505" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0076.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-104">{P{\rm av}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>The PCE decreases as frequency increases because the losses through the MOS capacitances increase with frequency, and their decreasing reactance reduces the transistors' drain currents, thus reducing the charging of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-105-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1506" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 2.646em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.345em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.35em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1507" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1508" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0043.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1509" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1510" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1511" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1512" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1513" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1514" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0064.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-105">C{\rm load}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>To enhance PCE at lower available power, external threshold voltage cancellation techniques, such as what is proposed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_4b">[17]</a> or zero-threshold voltage transistors as in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_4b">[18]</a>, should be used for lower diode drop. However, external <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-106-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1515" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.805em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.63em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1516" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1517" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0056.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1518" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1519" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1520" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0074.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1521" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0068.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-106">V{\rm th}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> cancellation or zero-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-107-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1522" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1525" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1526" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1527" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0074.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; An improved cross-coupled bridge structure as reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_4b">[19]</a> that combines zero-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-108-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1529" role="math" style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-108">V{\rm th}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> transistors to lower turn-on voltage, and four additional switches for reverse leakage current cancellation, should significantly improve PCE over a wider available power range (low, medium, and high <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-109-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1536" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.117em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1541" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1542" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1543" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1544" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0076.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; However, a technology that includes zero-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-110-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1545" role="math" style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-110">V{\rm th}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> RF model transistors is required.</p><p>From <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 5</a> – <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">7</a>, we can deduce a maximum measured overall PCE of 20%, 18%, and 11% at 24, 35, and 60 GHz, respectively, under a load resistor of 1 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-111-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1552" role="math" style="display: inline-block; Assuming an on-chip tag antenna of 6-dBi gain <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_4b">[10]</a> and a conservatively low RF power of 1-W EIRP (higher power will extend tag-reader communication range) transmitted from the reader, these rectifier characteristics demonstrate the feasibility of a fully integrated batteryless MMID tag with the downlink parameters (approximated using the Friis equation) and measured rectifier performances given in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>.

<p></p><p>Note that the values in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> assume a perfect line-of-sight alignment of reader and tag antenna beams. Any misalignment will result in conditions that deviate from the power budget associated to the values presented in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>.</p><p>In the conditions associated to the PCE maxima values in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>, the simulated input <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-113-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1568" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1569" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1570" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-113">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-114-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1571" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.745em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.5em 2.345em -999.997em); margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-115">S11</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are −5, −7, and −10 dB at 24, 35, and 60 GHz, respectively.</p><p>Note also that the measured results include the parasitic capacitances of the rectifier input pads. Impedance matching between the antenna and the rectifier should improve power transfer. However, careful tradeoff is required since matching circuit losses are significant at millimeter-wave frequencies and should be taken into account.</p><p>As can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>, compared to our design variant using narrower transistors with smaller parasitic capacitances and smaller leakage current, our design variant with wider transistors (with higher <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-116-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1579" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.505em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1580" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1581" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1582" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0049.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1583" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1584" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1585" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0073.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1586" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 6px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1587" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0074.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-116">I_{\rm sat}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) proved to be a better design centering for best efficiency as a function of the tradeoffs discussed in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A millimeter-wave rectifier for a batteryless active MMID tag, which can be remotely powered by a reader, has been designed and implemented in 65-nm CMOS technology. In addition to the small on-resistance and small leakage current achievable with a cross-coupled differential circuit, reducing transistor parasitic capacitances, series capacitor losses, and coupling between the on-chip metal lines are key factors for millimeter-wave rectifiers using a bulk CMOS process. The proposed rectifier achieves a PCE of 20% at 24 GHz, 18% at 35 GHz, and 11% at 60 GHz, under 6-dBm power driving for 24 and 35 GHz, and 3-dBm power driving for 60 GHz. These new results support the feasibility of the MMID reader-tag system proposed in this paper (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>), employing a batteryless “active” tag that is fully integrated on a single CMOS die, with no substrate, no die-attach, and no wiring.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGEMENT</h3><p>The authors would like to thank CMC Microsystems, Kingston, ON, Canada, for their support, tools, and chip fabrication.</p></div></div>

From 1996 to 1998, he was an RF Design Engineer with NEC, Melbourne, Australia, where he was involved with the development of RF and microwave transceivers for mobile telephony. From 1998 to 2002, he was a Design Engineer with Skyworks Solutions Inc., Newbury Park, CA, USA, where he developed GaAs HBT RFIC power amplifiers (PAs) for wireless communications. While with Skyworks Solutions Inc., he was also actively involved in research on smart biasing and efficiency improvement techniques for RFIC PAs. He holds three patents. His primary research interests are in the design and test of RFICs and front-end modules for wireless communications.</div><!-- end ngRepeat: biop in ::item.bio.p --><div class="pure-u-24-24 u-mt-1 ng-binding ng-scope" ng-repeat="biop in ::item.bio.p">Dr. Constantin was the recipient of a doctoral scholarship from the Natural Science and Engineering Research Council (NSERC) of Canada and a doctoral scholarship from ETS.</div><!-- end ngRepeat: biop in ::item.bio.p -->

He holds the first Cheung Kong endowed chair professorship (visiting) with Southeast University, the first Sir Yue-Kong Pao chair professorship (visiting) with Ningbo University, and an honorary professorship with the Nanjing University of Science and Technology, Nanjing University of Post and Telecommunication, and City University of Hong Kong. He has been the Director of the Poly-Grames Research Center and the founding Director of the Center for Radiofrequency Electronics Research of Quebec (Regroupement stratégique of FRQNT). He has also held guest and visiting professorships with many universities around the world. He has authored or coauthored over 950 referred papers and a number of books/book chapters. He has served on the editorial/review boards of many technical journals, transactions, proceedings, and letters, as well as scientific encyclopedias as an editor and guest editor. He has filed over 30 patents. His current research interests involve substrate integrated circuits (SICs), antenna arrays, advanced computer-aided design (CAD) and modeling techniques, wireless power transmission and harvesting, and development of low-cost RF and millimeter-wave transceivers and sensors for wireless systems and biomedical applications. He is also interested in the modeling and design of microwave photonic circuits and systems.</div><!-- end ngRepeat: biop in ::item.bio.p --><div class="pure-u-24-24 u-mt-1 ng-binding ng-scope" ng-repeat="biop in ::item.bio.p">Dr. Wu is a member of Electromagnetics Academy, Sigma Xi, and the URSI. He is a Fellow of the Canadian Academy of Engineering (CAE) and the Royal Society of Canada (The Canadian Academy of the Sciences and Humanities). He was an IEEE Microwave Theory and Techniques Society (IEEE MTT-S) Distinguished Microwave Lecturer from Jan. 2009 to Dec. 2011. He has held key positions in and has served on various panels and international committees including the chair of Technical Program Committees, international Steering Committees, and international conferences/symposia. In particular, he was the general chair of the 2012 IEEE MTT-S International Microwave Symposium (IMS). He is currently the chair of the joint IEEE chapters of MTT-S/AP-S/LEOS, Montreal, QC, Canada. He is an IEEE MTT-S Administrative Committee (AdCom) member (2006–2015) and has served as chair of the IEEE MTT-S Transnational Committee, Member and Geographic Activities (MGA) Committee, and Technical Coordinating Committee (TCC) among many other AdCom functions. He was the recipient of many awards and prizes including the first IEEE MTT-S Outstanding Young Engineer Award, the 2004 Fessenden Medal of the IEEE Canada, the 2009 Thomas W. Eadie Medal of the Royal Society of Canada, the Queen Elizabeth II Diamond Jubilee Medal in 2013, and the 2013 FCCP Education Foundation Award of Merit.</div><!-- end ngRepeat: biop in ::item.bio.p -->

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

</script>

It is a critical circuit block that renders possible the use of a single CMOS chip die with no substrate and wiring, as the implementation of a batteryless, yet active tag for next-generation high data-rate millimeter-wave identification technologies. We also propose an architecture of a reader-tag system that addresses the underlying technical challenges. The rectifier is based on a differential drive cross-coupled topology that has been shown to work at UHF frequencies only so far. In this paper, we investigate significant challenges in implementing this topology at millimeter-wave frequencies with good power conversion efficiency (PCE). The analyses, design, and results presented in this work demonstrate the feasibility of achieving this by minimizing simultaneously the small on-resistance and the reverse leakage current in the MOS transistors, and by reducing losses and parasitic capacitances through proper transistor sizing and layout optimization. Using a standard 65-nm bulk CMOS process, a chip was designed, fabricated, and tested under different input and output loading conditions. The rectifier exhibits an overall PCE of 20% at 24 GHz, 18% at 35 GHz, and 11% at 60 GHz under RF available driving power of 6, 6, and 3 dBm, respectively, and output load resistance of 1, 1, and 2 k&amp;#x03A9;, respectively. These PCE performances at millimeter-wave frequencies have never been reported in the
